<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer2585582777382888332">Matilda is a little girl who is far too good to be true. At age five-and-a-half she's knocking off double-digit multiplication problems and blitz-reading Dickens. Even more remarkably, her classmates love her even though she's a super-nerd and the teacher's pet. But everything is not perfect in Matilda's world. For starters she has two of the most idiotic, self-centered pa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2585582777382888332">Matilda is a little girl who is far too good to be true. At age five-and-a-half she's knocking off double-digit multiplication problems and blitz-reading Dickens. Even more remarkably, her classmates love her even though she's a super-nerd and the teacher's pet. But everything is not perfect in Matilda's world. For starters she has two of the most idiotic, self-centered parents who ever lived. Then there's the large, busty nightmare of a school principal, Mrs. ("The") Trunchbull, a former hammer-throwing champion who flings children at will and is approximately as sympathetic as a bulldozer. Fortunately for Matilda, she has the inner resources to deal with such annoyances: astonishing intelligence, saintly patience, and an innate predilection for revenge.<br /><br />She warms up with some practical jokes aimed at her hapless parents, but the true test comes when she rallies in defense of her teacher, the sweet Miss Honey, against the diabolical Trunchbull. There is never any doubt that Matilda will carry the day. Even so, this wonderful story is far from predictable. Roald Dahl, while keeping the plot moving imaginatively, also has an unerring ear for emotional truth. The reader cares about Matilda because in addition to all her other gifts, she has real feelings.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2585582777382888332">...more</a>

      </div>

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_6669').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();

      <a href="/user/show/18974711-darth-j" class="user" title="Darth J">Darth J</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/15812834-matilda" title="Hardcover 9780142424278" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=awesome" class="actionLinkLite">awesome</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/18974711-darth-j?shelf=would-recommend" class="actionLinkLite">would-recommend</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer583532435">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4541831552934261247"><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399917291ra/9609590.gif" /><br />While I personally love a book about a child prodigy (especially in the area of telekinesis), I had a different reaction to this book while rereading it as an adult. As a kid I thought Matilda was awesome, she was intelligent and independent. As an adult I see this as a book about gross neglect and a commentary on absentee parenting and its role in our children's education. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399917291ra/9609591.gif" /><br /><br />I come from a county where the dropout rate is high and everyone wants to blame the teachers, but no one identifies the rea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4541831552934261247"><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399917291ra/9609590.gif" /><br />While I personally love a book about a child prodigy (especially in the area of telekinesis), I had a different reaction to this book while rereading it as an adult. As a kid I thought Matilda was awesome, she was intelligent and independent. As an adult I see this as a book about gross neglect and a commentary on absentee parenting and its role in our children's education. <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399917291ra/9609591.gif" /><br /><br />I come from a county where the dropout rate is high and everyone wants to blame the teachers, but no one identifies the real problem of parents or caregivers not taking an active role in their child's schooling. To many of them, school is free babysitting and nothing more. They take no interest in helping their children succeed and tell the educators that it is their job to teach the children, disavowing any responsibility of their own. Once in a while you have a special case like Matilda who decides to work on her education on her own, despite the indifference of her parents. But more often these children turn into cases for Child Protective Services (or the equivalent) due to the negligence occurring in their home lives.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399917291ra/9609592.gif" /><br /><br />Matilda gets her happy ending, but most children in similar situations do not. Reread this as an adult with the above perspective and you will find a chilling tale of a child trying to create something better for herself than the toxic circumstances she was born into.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4541831552934261247">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/262259445?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5686305-shayantani-das" class="user" title="Shayantani Das">Shayantani Das</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5686305-shayantani-das?shelf=classic" class="actionLinkLite">classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5686305-shayantani-das?shelf=why-did-i-fall-for-this" class="actionLinkLite">why-did-i-fall-for-this</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer262259445">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5559651011080819168">Matilda is basically a child prodigy; she is 4 years old and a voracious reader. That is amazing, I know! But, Matilda is not the only character. There are the tyrannical parents who do not encourage reading, do not have a shred of love or sympathy for Matilda and basically hate Matilda for some unknown reason. They even abandon her without even thinking twice. Who does that???? Especially with out any sane cause. <br /><br />Then there is her school life and enters Mrs. Trunchbull. She is evil. Not simply</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5559651011080819168">Matilda is basically a child prodigy; she is 4 years old and a voracious reader. That is amazing, I know! But, Matilda is not the only character. There are the tyrannical parents who do not encourage reading, do not have a shred of love or sympathy for Matilda and basically hate Matilda for some unknown reason. They even abandon her without even thinking twice. Who does that???? Especially with out any sane cause. <br /><br />Then there is her school life and enters Mrs. Trunchbull. She is evil. Not simply evil, pure unadulterated evil. She goes about yanking people’s hair, pulling their ears and making their lives miserable. She loathes young kids, again without any reason. She is as one dimensional as a character can be . <br /><br /><br />I realize that it’s a children’s book and they don’t go about analyzing these things. Yes, I know it is not meant for my age group and so my opinion doesn’t matter and I didn’t consciously take out my microscope and start looking for flaws in this book. But still, the portrayal of teachers as well as parents is really disturbing.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_333049456">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333049456" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu" class="left imgcol" title="Jason Koivu"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1440701539p2/1742824.jpg" alt="Jason Koivu" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/333049456?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu" class="user" title="Jason Koivu">Jason Koivu</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=comedy" class="actionLinkLite">comedy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer333049456">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4429052237216712078">This might be one of the most perfect books for readers. It's about a reader who just wants to get her read on and bad people are trying to stop her. <br /><br />Instant character attachment! <br /><br />Fully involved in the "tumultuous" plot!<br /><br />"<em>Let my reader goooo....</em>" sing the readers!<br /><br />What a wonderful tale! Little Matilda is saddled with a nasty father, a fairly terrible mother and an indifferent brother. Matilda just wants to read. Why read when we've got the telly, wonder her disgusting parents. After being crapped</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4429052237216712078">This might be one of the most perfect books for readers. It's about a reader who just wants to get her read on and bad people are trying to stop her. <br /><br />Instant character attachment! <br /><br />Fully involved in the "tumultuous" plot!<br /><br />"<em>Let my reader goooo....</em>" sing the readers!<br /><br />What a wonderful tale! Little Matilda is saddled with a nasty father, a fairly terrible mother and an indifferent brother. Matilda just wants to read. Why read when we've got the telly, wonder her disgusting parents. After being crapped on enough times, Matilda begins taking out her revenge in the whip-smartest ways and so ensues the fun!<br /><br />Dahl's style is all over this. His bad guys are awfully bad, I mean really wonderfully rotten. His hero is intelligent and intrepid, with Dahl no doubt using his secret agent background to infuse even the simplest fairytale with spy-craft cunning. His story is episodic. You can see the acts/scenes play out with definitive beginnings and ends, as if he wrote a handful of short stories and plugged them into one book. <br /><br />Negatives include some unbelievably bad bad guy moments that leave us boring adult readers thinking, "well <em>that</em> could never happen"...because we're dumb. Also, I don't think this needed the dip it takes into magical fantasy. It was doing perfectly fine without it. I rather liked that Matilda was solving her problems on her own without a supernatural assistance. It was more impressive. <br /><br />Lots of adult subject matter herein (Suicide?!...shit dude, that's heavy) and I was taken back a bit at first. This is a kid's book after all. But I guess even I'd forgotten that kid's books used to dish out the tough stuff back in the old days. Now it's all about princesses and pretty pretty rainbow ponies, and if one of them gets a cold, it's a fucking big deal.<br /><br />I was considering reading this to my niece, who just turned six, so I wanted to pre-read it first to make sure it was suitable. I wasn't actually worried about the subject matter (and I'm still not), I was more concerned about the length. She's not into long books yet, you see. Not much of an attention span on that girl, but I'm partly to blame. Historically speaking, when she's come to visit it becomes a whirlwind of "WHAT DO WE DO NEXT!!!", because when she was about 3 to 5 years old I just wanted to keep her entertained. I might've gone overboard. She's come to expect a circus for every visit to my house. Nonetheless, having finally read <em>Matilda</em> and knowing how much my niece loves to read, I do believe this will soon become an absolute favorite of hers as it as has so quickly become one of mine. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4429052237216712078">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">cool people</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariel by: </span>
      public school
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9721342">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14162776156043625213">"You chose books and I chose looks." Matilda's mom kills me. I chose looks. I like to look smart too, though. In high school my bro's friends would pick on me for owning so many books. I pretended to be dumb like Matilda and said I hadn't read any of the books and they were trophies to make me look smart. That answer was apparently the right thing to say (probably about the only time I've ever said the right thing either. If it is right to say either like eye-ther I said it like eee-thur, and so</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14162776156043625213">"You chose books and I chose looks." Matilda's mom kills me. I chose looks. I like to look smart too, though. In high school my bro's friends would pick on me for owning so many books. I pretended to be dumb like Matilda and said I hadn't read any of the books and they were trophies to make me look smart. That answer was apparently the right thing to say (probably about the only time I've ever said the right thing either. If it is right to say either like eye-ther I said it like eee-thur, and so forth). (Scary glimpse into my mind, I conciously pronounce it both ways so I'll have a percentage chance of getting it right.)<br /><br />One of my favorite childhood books. I can't remember anything good about grade school that wasn't reading Roald Dahl (and a few other not-Roald-Dahl-peoples, to be fair *mutters*). My other memories are stuff like getting puked on and having to wear (all day!) nasty clothes from the '70s from the lost and found. I remember this boy my twin and I absolutely loathed 'cause he ate tuna fish sandwiches with his mouth open (yuck!). We'd go home at the end of the day and pool stories of the day about nasty stuff like that. One of the classes we were allowed to share (public school systems apparently believe in seperating twins. Bastards. It's not like we were gonna form a group and hate people together...oh, wait) was English class. I loved it when Lauren got her turn to read aloud. She did the best ever Matilda's mom. My favorite characters were the nasty ones like Matilda's parents. The funny nasty ones. Trunchbull was disgusting. She actually kept kids in an iron maiden type thing. Vicious! I love Roald Dahl. He'd have hated tuna fish sandwiches and that disgusting '80s fad of "a train going through a tunnel", fo' sho.<br /><br />I can't believe the big deal made about margarine versus butter. My mom was permanently on a diet and I cannot drink real milk to this day (yes, I know that skim milk is basically white water). Same deal for margarine. I might not have ever had real butter. So what if Miss Honey had real butter? She had food! That also appealed to me greatly as a kid, 'cause we were not allowed to have anything that might tempt my mother away from her diets (she broke them in secret and hid the evidence. Meanie). I remember reading <em>Matilda</em> and getting hungry over all the food stuff. <em>The Twits</em> didn't make me hungry (my bird is shooting me nervous glances right about now, in case I get any pie making ideas). Roald Dahl wouldn't have starved his kids 'cause he wanted to look hot for book jacket photo shoots.<br /><br />p.s. <em>The Twits</em> is my favorite Roald Dahl book.<br />p.s.s. <em>James and the Giant Peach</em> is also really great. The only time I didn't hate my classmates (we had feuds over <em>The Teenage Mutant Ninja Turtles</em>) was when we related to loving Roald Dahl. Except they sucked at reading aloud so I really did still hate their guts.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14162776156043625213">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12570010633024273717"><em>All the reading she had done had given her a view of life that they had never seen.</em><br /><br />This book was so heartwarming. And it just proved that Dahl was (and always will be) one of the best storytellers ever. The way he writes and how he draws you into the story will always amaze me. This is my second book of his, but it definitely won't be my last.<br /><br />Amazing book, that I think everybody should read, at least once.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/18321322-sarah-churchill?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer873922299">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer762124846028331420">What's not to love about Matilda? Child genius who loves reading and learning, Terrible (verbally abusive) parents and an all kinds of abusive Headmistress. It sounds like it's going to be dismal, and it is sad - I really, really felt for little Matilda - but her attitude and outlook on life are fantastic and inspirational. And like all Dahl books, the nasty characters get their comeuppance. Love, love, love this book even more than I remembered.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1203245289">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5640103238155941354">WOW, I loved <strong> <a title="Matilda by Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39988.Matilda">Matilda</a> </strong>! This was my first time reading the story that makes so many list of "must read" that I wanted to understand what all of the fuss was about. Well now I do!!!<br /><br /><strong><a title="Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">Roald Dahl</a> </strong>weaves a compelling and creative tale that keeps the reader interested from start to finish! This book is charming, clever, and funny ... with a bit of sadness mixed in.<br /><br />The characters are vividly developed: <br /><br />From the Good ...<br /><br />* Matilda, the child prodigy, who taught herself to read and has morals (not sure whe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5640103238155941354">WOW, I loved <strong>
  <a title="Matilda by Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39988.Matilda">Matilda</a>
</strong>! This was my first time reading the story that makes so many list of "must read" that I wanted to understand what all of the fuss was about. Well now I do!!!<br /><br /><strong><a title="Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">Roald Dahl</a> </strong>weaves a compelling and creative tale that keeps the reader interested from start to finish! This book is charming, clever, and funny ... with a bit of sadness mixed in.<br /><br />The characters are vividly developed: <br /><br />From the Good ...<br /><br />* Matilda, the child prodigy, who taught herself to read and has morals (not sure where they came from)<br />* Miss Honey, the teacher, who is the first adult who takes an interest in advancing Matilda and is the first person to show her love<br /><br />...To the Bad <br /><br />* Matilda's father, an unethical car dealer, who delights in cheating customers <br />* Matilda's mother, a "housewife", who watches bad television and plays daily bingo (while leaving her kids to fend for themselves)<br />* Miss Trunchbull, the evil headmistress of Matilda's school, who delights in tormenting all of the students and visits each of the classes once a week to deliver outlandish punishments<br /><br />I won't go farther into the plot, as there are many reviews out there that probably say it better!<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who has a sense of humor and a heart. It is a quick and fun read! I will be reading the other Dahl books that I have missed in the near future!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ I love that the book ended with Miss Trunchbull returning the house to Miss Honey (rightful owner) and leaving the school. Also, that Matilda and Miss Honey end up together in the end, with Matilda's family fleeing the country and not caring if she stays back. Happily ever after!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_204445507">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204445507" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="left imgcol" title="K.D. Absolutely"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449978413p2/2156200.jpg" alt="K.D. Absolutely" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/204445507?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 14, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="user" title="K.D. Absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/109059.Matilda" title="Paperback 9780142410370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/726059-dante">Dante</a>
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=humour" class="actionLinkLite">humour</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=book-club" class="actionLinkLite">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer204445507">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3699230449076663484">This is my third book by Roald Dahi (1916-1990). I did not plan to read this because I’ve already read his more famous (earlier) <em>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</em> (1964) and his boyhood memoir, <em>Boy: Tales of Childhood</em> (1984) which are both included in the <em>501 Must Read Books</em> that I am trying to read completely. However, the Filipinos group here in Goodreads selected this book as its bestseller read for this month, September 2011 so I had to buy and read this one too.<br /><br />This book's main protagonist,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3699230449076663484">This is my third book by Roald Dahi (1916-1990). I did not plan to read this because I’ve already read his more famous (earlier) <em>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</em> (1964) and his boyhood memoir, <em>Boy: Tales of Childhood</em> (1984) which are both included in the <em>501 Must Read Books</em> that I am trying to read completely. However, the Filipinos group here in Goodreads selected this book as its bestseller read for this month, September 2011 so I had to buy and read this one too.<br /><br />This book's main protagonist, <strong>Matilda</strong> is a precocious, smart and telekinetic 4-y/o book lover who puts super glue on the inside lining of his father’s hat so her mother has to cut the hat and the hair of the poor father so he can sleep properly. I am sure some women, for whatever strange reason, find this funny. However, for a father like me, it is definitely not. No one, fathers included, is perfect. Even if Matilda’s father is mean, obnoxious, shouts at Matilda or does not agree to buy her books and asks her to watch the television instead, he is the one putting food on the dining table. Matilda has to respect his parents. This also includes his mother who, even if she is insensitive, who leaves Matilda all by herself at home every afternoon to play bingo, at least, does not physically hurt or starve her to death. Hence, Matilda has no right to disrespect her parents including scaring them by hiding a parrot up in the chimney, even if the parrot is as lovable as the one in the book. I know that this book is intended for children and most of my GR friends say that they read and liked when they were young (this came out in 1988) so my griping or nitpicking is totally misplaced as I am now an old dog. But hey, I will not tell my teen daughter or my very young nieces to read this as I don't see Matilda as a good girl role model for them. Try Dorothy in <em>The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</em> or even maybe Pippi Longstocking but definitely not Matilda.<br /><br />The other reason why I find this book inferior Dahl's other works like <em>Charlie</em> and <em>Boy</em> is the one-dimensional character of the antagonist, headmistress <strong>Miss Trunchbull</strong>. Why did she become nasty? I understand that the headmistress is not the highest official of a British school, so what do the other school authorities are saying about Miss Trunchbull’s behavior towards the students? Granting that <strong>Miss Honey</strong> is afraid of her, considering that the other children are not afraid to talk, are they not saying anything to their parents who in turn can get in touch with the other school authorities or even the police?<br /><br />However, I cannot fully dislike this novel. Any booklover main character is hard for me not to love. Dahl’s children’s books are mostly based on actual people and experiences that he met or had when he was a young boy as his memoir <em>Boy: Tales of Childhood</em> stated. As examples, Miss Trunchbull’s character is said to be based on an actual nasty teacher he had in British school or the conteest entries to the chocolate factory in <em>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</em> were based on real life chocolate recipe contests used to sponsored by Cadbury during his childhood years in England. Also, the relationship of Matilda and Miss Honey should have been inspired by the homesickness that Dahl experienced at British school while he was away from his mom. Aww, sweet boy.<br /><br />This book is not really bad. I only thought that <em>Charlie</em> and <em>Boy</em> better written, more truthful and more inspiring. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3699230449076663484">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/3518073?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 25, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/220219-heron" class="user" title="Heron">Heron</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer3518073">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6609309192467492790">Oh <a title=" Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Roald%20Dahl"> Roald Dahl</a>, you make my life complete. Matilda is one of <em>those</em> books for me. One of the books in my bookshelf, tattered and worn, pages falling out, that I will always go back to, no matter what the occasion. Dear, darling Miss Honey, Matilda's first grade teacher, is ever child's dream, and now that I'm older, every adult's dream as well. Miss Honey lives in a two room cottage with no running water, a camp stove, and wooden boxes for seats. She eats margarine instead of butter! Would that w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6609309192467492790">Oh <a title=" Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Roald%20Dahl"> Roald Dahl</a>, you make my life complete. Matilda is one of <em>those</em> books for me. One of the books in my bookshelf, tattered and worn, pages falling out, that I will always go back to, no matter what the occasion. Dear, darling Miss Honey, Matilda's first grade teacher, is ever child's dream, and now that I'm older, every adult's dream as well. Miss Honey lives in a two room cottage with no running water, a camp stove, and wooden boxes for seats. She eats margarine instead of butter! Would that we all could be so jolly under such circumstances, and still be able to stick it to the man- the man in this case being Miss Trunchbull, the evil (truly) headmistress and incidentally, Miss Honey's aunt. I used to dream of being so smart that I could lift cigars with my mind. But now I dream of being able to influence just one little girl's life for the better. Thank you, Mr. Dahl. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1449837744">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1449837744" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/23304719-anne-anneshka" class="left imgcol" title="Anne (Anneshka)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451613103p2/23304719.jpg" alt="Anne (Anneshka)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1449837744?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/23304719-anne-anneshka" class="user" title="Anne (Anneshka)">Anne (Anneshka)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/23304719-anne-anneshka?shelf=the-kid-in-me" class="actionLinkLite">the-kid-in-me</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/23304719-anne-anneshka?shelf=classics" class="actionLinkLite">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1449837744">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6448810912772298804"><strong> Matilda, little as she is, is an inspiration </strong><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449024740ra/17224583.gif" /><br /><br /><strong>Matilda</strong> is an exceptional girl, ridiculously brilliant, a voracious reader, and self-sufficient even at the early age of four years...and three months. The story? She's born into a <strong>horrible</strong> and <strong>negligent </strong>family too disdainful to see her worth.<br /><br /><strong>I did enjoy this book,</strong> <em>but</em> I was a little unimpressed by it. Maybe it's because I've already watched the movie, and it was a good movie honestly. The pranks carried out by <strong>Matilda</strong> <br /> were quite humorous in written</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6448810912772298804"><strong> Matilda, little as she is, is an inspiration </strong><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449024740ra/17224583.gif" /><br /><br /><strong>Matilda</strong> is an exceptional girl, ridiculously brilliant, a voracious reader, and self-sufficient even at the early age of four years...and three months. The story? She's born into a <strong>horrible</strong> and <strong>negligent </strong>family too disdainful to see her worth.<br /><br /><strong>I did enjoy this book,</strong> <em>but</em> I was a little unimpressed by it. Maybe it's because I've already watched the movie, and it was a good movie honestly. The pranks carried out by <strong>Matilda</strong> <br /> were quite humorous in written form, but watching them acted out on screen was ultimately better. <strong>
  <u>But that's just how I feel </u>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>How I loved,</strong> loved Matilda's vibrant character!<br /><em>The only thing</em> that caused me to cringe slightly was her taste for Ovaltine. Ugh, I hated that stuff. I could never even call it a beverage. I don't know, it always tasted like medicine to me. What to do? I've got a weird tongue.<br /><br /><strong>
  <u>WHAT REALLY MATTERS TO ME... </u>
</strong><br /><strong>I think Matilda's father's attitude </strong>towards her reading lifestyle can symbolize the general attitude and reaction of non-readers to readership<strong>(I really do hate generalizations, but I think I can be excused in my application of it in this matter) </strong><br /><strong>Most people </strong> can't begin to understand why I would "slave" over words, and worry pages of books. <strong>How could I not be bored?</strong> I'm accustomed to the routine head shakes and murmurings of how helpless my situation is whenever they ask me what I'm doing Friday night and I answer,<strong> "I'll be in bed, with a book".</strong> Granted, most aren't as malicious as Matilda's father to the cause, but they aren't as tolerant or forgiving<em>--as if reading and books are things to be endured.</em><br /><br /><strong>People aren't so critical </strong>nowadays to the topic of reading. I remember my father telling me about how his sister(my aunt) would lock herself in the toilet with a book because she had to hide to read. Their mother wasn't so keen about her having her nose in a book all the time. Absurd, I know. I couldn't believe it initially. I can't imagine being told that I couldn't read. <br /><br /><strong> I'm tempted </strong>to give this one a higher rating because though I wasn't blown away by the story, the underlying theme merits it, for me. But I want things to be honest so I'll go with what I <strong>really</strong> feel like giving.<br /><br /><strong>That said, </strong>this simple children's book gives us something we all can identify with as readers. This is a tribute to readers.<em> It's a tribute to the</em><strong> world </strong><em>between</em><strong> book pages.</strong> <strong>Roald Dahl</strong> <s>is</s> was just too good a <strong>writer</strong> and<strong> storyteller.</strong> Add him to the list of people I'll never get a chance to meet. <br /><strong>3.5/5 stars</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6448810912772298804">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4494694682754344055">This was a fun read, even though the movie Matilda is heavily engraved in my mind and there was no real surprises when reading it. It was fun even though the young lad I was reading it with kept falling asleep two pages in, and I felt to finish in one night. <br />This story could be used as a manual to parents on how to NOT raise your kids and to all the Trunchbottoms, on how to Not teach children. <br />All the Trunchbottoms watch out their next pupil might just be like Matilda or up the ante maybe the gi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4494694682754344055">This was a fun read, even though the movie Matilda is heavily engraved in my mind and there was no real surprises when reading it. It was fun even though the young lad I was reading it with kept falling asleep two pages in, and I felt to finish in one night. <br />This story could be used as a manual to parents on how to NOT raise your kids and to all the Trunchbottoms, on how to Not teach children. <br />All the Trunchbottoms watch out their next pupil might just be like Matilda or up the ante maybe the girl Drew Barrymore played in The Firestarter adaptation of Stephen Kings novel. It also highlights the joy and the value of having a good and kind teacher like that which Matilda successfully had. Last but not least the joy of reading Matilda displayed was a real billboard advertisement for the promotion of reading to young kids and left a lasting importance for many.<br />Truly a great writer who can be remembered as being in many readers bedtime stories.<br />There is a sort of hall of fame of gifted young girls that she joins alongside Firestarter girl and Swan from Swan song by Robert McCammon.<br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s1184.photobucket.com/albums/z322/LouPendergrast/?action=view&amp;current=bdc1037a.jpg">

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_236834799">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236834799" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4740396-sj" class="left imgcol" title="sj"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1384356482p2/4740396.jpg" alt="sj" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/236834799?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4740396-sj" class="user" title="sj">sj</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer236834799">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8467709151852879489">My senior year in high school, I became friends with this girl that kind of way outclassed me.<br /><br />I wore men's cords and snap up western shirts under tee shirts, and was often barefoot when I could get away with it (I kept my duct taped corduroy converse in my backpack and would just slip them on when I went into class)I dyed my hair every week and went to a lot of local punk and third wave shows (srsly, a lot - like at least two a week and I rarely paid my way in).<br /><br />Contrast with E. who wore heels an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8467709151852879489">My senior year in high school, I became friends with this girl that kind of way outclassed me.<br /><br />I wore men's cords and snap up western shirts under tee shirts, and was often barefoot when I could get away with it (I kept my duct taped corduroy converse in my backpack and would just slip them on when I went into class)I dyed my hair every week and went to a lot of local punk and third wave shows (srsly, a lot - like at least two a week and I rarely paid my way in).<br /><br />Contrast with E. who wore heels and dresses (I was <em>shocked</em> the first time I saw her in pants) every day, had Lucy red hair and perfectly sculpted eyebrows.<br /><br />I didn't understand how she could want to be my friend (much like I still am today, really), but we were super tight for a while.<br /><br />I met her through a kindasorta friend of mine that had a crush on her, and he thought they were dating, when they totally weren't. Anyway, we were hanging out at T.'s house and she and I were talking and totally ignoring him.<br /><br />She looked me up and down and I felt really uncomfortable being scrutinized, then said that she didn't think my name suited me. I had always hated my name (I've got one of those super common late-70s names, for realsies - it was the most common female name the year I was born) and when she told me that I seemed more like a <em>Matilda</em> to her, I was thrilled.<br /><br />I even let her make me over and would spend Sunday nights at her house (our school started 2 hours later every Monday) and she'd curl my hair and dress me up (oh, because WE WERE THE SAME HEIGHT AND BOTH HAD GIANT FEET) and [gasp] put makeup on me.<br /><br />Those Sunday nights/Monday mornings where I got to be Matilda were some of the only good parts of that year, and every time I see this book, I think of her.<br /><br />Of COURSE I was a huge Dahl fan when I was growing up, and I empathized so hard with little Matilda, whose parents were total selfish assholes. How I longed for a Miss Honey in my life.<br /><br />[sigh]<br /><br />Oh, and if you're interested you can hit the spoiler tag for one of the few photos of me at that age that I don't actually hate.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Actually, I had to remove the photo cos some weirdos were looking at it too much and ended up using most of my screencast bandwidth. FIVE THOUSAND VIEWS IN A MONTH?! Um...it wasn't even a very good picture, creeps. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10953256123119374681">La verdad es que siempre tuve curiosidad por leer este libro ya que siempre amé la peli, pero la honestamente esperaba otra cosas y resultó no ser mi favorito de Roald Dahl, tiene obras mucho más ingeniosas y entretenidas.<br /><br />Lo dejo en un me gustó.<br /><br />Sin embargo, le voy a dar cinco estrellas porque:<br /><br />1º es Roald Dahl<br />2º es Matilda<br />3º detesto a los adultos que le dan puntajes negativos a libros infantiles. Dios no permita que me convierta en una alguna vez :P<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_138729887">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138729887" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist" class="left imgcol" title="Jeanette  &quot;Astute Crabbist&quot;"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1304653755p2/796425.jpg" alt="Jeanette  &quot;Astute Crabbist&quot;" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/138729887?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 05, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist" class="user" title="Jeanette  &quot;Astute Crabbist&quot;">Jeanette  "Astute Crabbist"</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6669.Matilda" title="Paperback 9780142402535" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=giggles" class="actionLinkLite">giggles</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=five-star-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">five-star-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=young-adult-books" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=all-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">all-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/796425-jeanette-astute-crabbist?shelf=for-the-munchkins" class="actionLinkLite">for-the-munchkins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer138729887">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6425994145714343096">I have to wonder about Roald Dahl's childhood. His evil adult characters <em>had</em> to have come from his own nightmares. The kids always win against the grownups, though. Maybe that's why Dahl's books are so popular. Isn't it every kid's dream to get back at the big people who get to control your life just because they're big and you're little? <br />Some of Dahl's grownups are so absurdly cruel, it emphasizes the fact that there are a lot of adults who should not be allowed near children. (I'm thinking of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6425994145714343096">I have to wonder about Roald Dahl's childhood. His evil adult characters <em>had</em> to have come from his own nightmares. The kids always win against the grownups, though. Maybe that's why Dahl's books are so popular. Isn't it every kid's dream to get back at the big people who get to control your life just because they're big and you're little? <br />Some of Dahl's grownups are so absurdly cruel, it emphasizes the fact that there are a lot of adults who should not be allowed near children. (I'm thinking of Mrs. Nail, my first grade teacher. Yes, I <em>am</em> still bitter!) <br /><br />Matilda is an extremely precocious little girl with idiotic parents. She finds hilarious ways to get back at them for treating her badly, and they're too stupid to figure out she's the culprit. When she's old enough to go to school, she encounters the headmistress known as The Trunchbull. The Trunchbull is the meanest of the mean. She's even worse than the aunts in <em>James and the Giant Peach</em>. She picks kids up by their hair and swings and flings them. She's so bad that I'd classify this as a YA book rather than children's. <br />When The Trunchbull unleashes her abuse on Matilda's class, Matilda discovers a special power that gets rid of the Trunchbull forever. Next time I see a kid staring intently at something, I'll think they're trying to move it with their eyes. I <em>know</em> I would have tried it constantly if I'd read this book as a child. Maybe I still will try it. One never knows...<br />Matilda really hits the jackpot, because she also gets to ditch her lousy parents and brother, and live happily ever after with her beloved teacher, Miss Honey.<br /><br />I give this 4.5 stars, but I'm not feeling stingy enough to nitpick over half a star. Besides, it held me spellbound, so that's worth extra points. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6425994145714343096">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1288474865">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288474865" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9077850-molly" class="left imgcol" title="Molly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1345305363p2/9077850.jpg" alt="Molly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1288474865?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9077850-molly" class="user" title="Molly">Molly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=paranormal" class="actionLinkLite">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1288474865">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11595446755969026759"><u>Rating, 2.5</u> (No, it's not a typo, it would have been a rating of 1.5, but I loved the beginning and Matilda discovering her love for books.)<br /><br />Oh, please <u>don't bash me. I really wished to love this book</u>. I was sure I would. It's a children's book everyone loves .... everyone but me. Sorry. <br /><br /><u>WARNING!</u> Seriously incoherent ranting ahead. Spoilers too. I don't care.<br /><br /><img height="221" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451928023ra/17622699.gif" /><br /><br />Matilda is a precocious five old girl, who loooves reading (how great is that). She's very smart and down to earth. She has the most OBNOXIO</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11595446755969026759"><u>Rating, 2.5</u> (No, it's not a typo, it would have been a rating of 1.5, but I loved the beginning and Matilda discovering her love for books.)<br /><br />Oh, please <u>don't bash me. I really wished to love this book</u>. I was sure I would. It's a children's book everyone loves .... everyone but me. Sorry. <br /><br /><u>WARNING!</u> Seriously incoherent ranting ahead. Spoilers too. I don't care.<br /><br /><img height="221" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451928023ra/17622699.gif" /><br /><br />Matilda is a precocious five old girl, who loooves reading (how great is that). She's very smart and down to earth. She has the most OBNOXIOUS parents (especially her dad), the most supportive teacher and has to put up with a child-hating, bone-chilling headmistress. Reading the book we see how she gets to outsmart her parents, how she saves the school and her favorite teacher, the sweet Miss Honey from the rule of the deranged school headmistress Mrs. Trunchbull, with smarts and paranormal powers (Yes, you've heard me right).<br /><br /><img height="221" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451928023ra/17622700.gif" /><br /><br />Matilda with her smarts reminds me of Kevin from the movie Home Alone (with the addition of terrible parents and paranormal powers). You see, I loved that kind of smarts in that movie (watched it more times I want to admit) ... and find them cringe-worthy in the book (I have double standards, I know).<br />Matilda's dad is a prick (no doubt about that), that cheats and yells and rips books apart (*gasp* for that, I wanted to smack him), but her super-gluing his hat on his head, or putting hydrogen peroxide in his hair lotion ... I don't know ... what are we teaching kids now ... let's mess with chemicals when our parents are tools (or when we think they are).<br /><br />This is a book for children. Obviously. What is Mr. Dahl teaching kids here? I get that this is just a fun story (like Home Alone) not to be taken to seriously, yet.... I get that her parents are insufferable. I get that The Trunchbull is almost demonic in her ways .... and that Miss Honey is a sweet, sweet teacher, but ...<br /><br />I cringed at the fact that the parents were painted like the worst. I know there are all kinds of "parents" out there. But come on Mr. Dahl. It's a book for kids. Couldn't you've given us just a glimpse of change or appreciation towards their daughter? A glimmer of redemption? No? <br /><br /><img height="201" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451928023ra/17622701.gif" /><br /><br />Alright, let's say that her parents are irredeemable (there are good-for-nothing parents out there), but ... there's more.<br /><br />I know that Matilda is smart for her age, but ... she follows blindly her teacher in some remote shack, with bare walls and three wooden boxes for furniture. The teacher the sends five year old Matilda to fetch water from a well... for tea. WTF. My late grandma had one in the front garden, and no way was I permitted going near it without supervision. Matilda stays for tea, listening her teacher unburdening her problems on her. Yes, yes I know, Matilda is super smart for her age, but in what world a twenty-something adult dumps her life's misery on a five-year-old girl.<br /><br /><img height="340" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451928023ra/17622702.gif" /><br /><br />So, kids, all parents are horrible, sweet talking strangers are great ... don't forget to follow them when they guide you in some secluded shack, and than drink what they give you, listen to their adult problems, do everything in your power to please them and then leave your family behind. Parents are no good (those of the other kids in school were hardly better than Matilda's). Long live sweet-talking strangers!<br /><br />Now I wish to forget this mess .... please.<br /><br /><img height="234" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451928023ra/17622703.gif" /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11595446755969026759">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2013" class="actionLinkLite">read2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer696650367">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3377358262706782024">Despite Roald Dahl being my <em>favorite</em> author as a child (I loved <a title="The BFG by Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6319.The_BFG">The BFG</a> and <a title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a> the most), I never read this book as a child. I've also never seen the movie. I suspect my parents kept it from me, afraid of what my brain would do with the revenge fantasy theme. *grin* I do love the idea of extra brain power coming out in secret powers. I already had that fantasy as a child, so my parents couldn't keep it from me entirely.<br /><br />This audiobook production is spectacular. Kate</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3377358262706782024">Despite Roald Dahl being my <em>favorite</em> author as a child (I loved <a title="The BFG by Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6319.The_BFG">The BFG</a> and <a title="Charlie and the Chocolate Factory (Charlie Bucket, #1) by Roald Dahl" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6310.Charlie_and_the_Chocolate_Factory__Charlie_Bucket___1_">Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</a> the most), I never read this book as a child. I've also never seen the movie. I suspect my parents kept it from me, afraid of what my brain would do with the revenge fantasy theme. *grin* I do love the idea of extra brain power coming out in secret powers. I already had that fantasy as a child, so my parents couldn't keep it from me entirely.<br /><br />This audiobook production is spectacular. Kate Winslet is great at all the characters, and it becomes clear rather quickly how much yelling the evil adults do to try to assert their control. The best scene in the book is the chocolate cake scene, and she brings even more life to it.<br /><br />One thing I love about this book is the portrayal of the librarian at the beginning. She isn't forbidding, she isn't so staunchly a rule-follower that she can't help a tiny girl, and her willingness to help a child changes Matilda's life. Hooray for librarians!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3377358262706782024">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/10703426?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 16, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/98734-nico" class="user" title="Nico">Nico</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/98734-nico?shelf=childhood-confessional" class="actionLinkLite">childhood-confessional</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer10703426">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7036764183597339090">This book was almost *too* stimulating, too gloriously gratifying, when first I read it at a tender age: it's repulsively trite of me to say this, but I felt that it had been written expressly for me.<br /><br />Just a few of its attractions:<br /> - a fiendishly, freakishly precocious protagonist, whose precocity is depicted as a source of both value and supernatural powers. We're supposed to love Matilda *because* she's smart (a welcome relief from the nerd-bashing and suffocating averageness of other kids'-lit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7036764183597339090">This book was almost *too* stimulating, too gloriously gratifying, when first I read it at a tender age: it's repulsively trite of me to say this, but I felt that it had been written expressly for me.<br /><br />Just a few of its attractions:<br /> - a fiendishly, freakishly precocious protagonist, whose precocity is depicted as a source of both value and supernatural powers. We're supposed to love Matilda *because* she's smart (a welcome relief from the nerd-bashing and suffocating averageness of other kids'-lit heroes, in those bad old pre-Potter Dark Ages);<br /><br /> - Matilda's triumphant emancipation from and victory over her hateful, Philistine, raping-and-pillaging parents, followed by the most agonizingly exciting development of all, to wit:<br /><br /> - the fact that Matilda gets to rescue a preternaturally alluring damsel in distress -- her teacher, the hauntingly named Miss Olivia Honey. Miss Honey is, quite simply, a high femme goddess for the juice-box set, and she featured prominently in my sexual fantasies until at least the age of seventeen;<br /><br /> - Matilda gets the girl at the end -- the last page of the book shows the two embracing, anticipatory to moving into Miss Honey's ancestral mansion, where presumably they will delight in the massive library, the tasteful appointments, and each other.<br /><br />When Matilda reaches her majority, of course.<br /><br />God I love this book. The pleasures of identification and wish fulfillment are quite heady indeed.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7036764183597339090">...more</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer649185210">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1914727443726832151">June 23, 2013<br /><br />Another wonderful memory of my childhood. Sort of. I read this book years ago (I won't say how many, of course), and I loved it. My dear grandma (my Goodreads back then) bought it for me. I read it as fast as I read <a title="Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_">Little Women</a>. I just couldn't put it away. Amazing story, nice writing, funny descriptions of... kind of awkward situations. Really good book. A book that I no longer have because I lent it to someone and that someone NEVER gave it back to me. So, if you, "someone", have</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1914727443726832151">June 23, 2013<br /><br />Another wonderful memory of my childhood. Sort of. I read this book years ago (I won't say how many, of course), and I loved it. My dear grandma (my Goodreads back then) bought it for me. I read it as fast as I read <a title="Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_">Little Women</a>. I just couldn't put it away. Amazing story, nice writing, funny descriptions of... kind of awkward situations. Really good book. A book that I no longer have because I lent it to someone and that someone NEVER gave it back to me. So, if you, "someone", have this book and you do not remember buying it, that means it is MY book which you know it was not given as a freaking present because I loved it but I wanted you to read it so you could love it too and then maybe buy your damn copy!<br /><br />Yes, that is why it is not such a wonderful memory, I guess.<br /><br />Anyway, that was therapeutic.<br /><br /><br />***<br /><br />July 12, 2014<br /><br />I wanted to clarify that, yesterday, after so many years, and just because that person saw me the other day and "remembered", I have my Matilda copy back. Its beautiful pages are now so, so yellow and sad. Now, it will receive the care it deserves. <br />I do not like lending my books. I do not trust humanity with <strong>my</strong> books, anymore!</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453863967" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass" class="left imgcol" title="Sonja - Intellectual Badass"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451471115p2/35853271.jpg" alt="Sonja - Intellectual Badass" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1453863967?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 10, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass" class="user" title="Sonja - Intellectual Badass">Sonja - Intellectual Badass</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/109019.Matilda" title="Hardcover 9780435123987" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass?shelf=awesomesauce" class="actionLinkLite">awesomesauce</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass?shelf=classic" class="actionLinkLite">classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass?shelf=contemporary" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass?shelf=childrens" class="actionLinkLite">childrens</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass?shelf=family" class="actionLinkLite">family</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/35853271-sonja---intellectual-badass?shelf=relationships" class="actionLinkLite">relationships</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1453863967">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer96448085524101926"><em>Matilda</em> is a childhood favourite of mine. When I saw it in my school's library I couldn't resist rereading it. I was browsing through the relatively small section of English books when my eyes settled on a row of books. Roald Dahl's books. My eyes swept over the books, zeroing in one particular book.<em> Matilda</em>.<br /><br />For me, <em>Matilda</em> was a classroom filled with enthralled children, each one waiting to hear what was going to happen next. It was laughter and tears. It was the way my teacher lifted her glass</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText96448085524101926"><em>Matilda</em> is a childhood favourite of mine. When I saw it in my school's library I couldn't resist rereading it. I was browsing through the relatively small section of English books when my eyes settled on a row of books. Roald Dahl's books. My eyes swept over the books, zeroing in one particular book.<em> Matilda</em>.<br /><br />For me, <em>Matilda</em> was a classroom filled with enthralled children, each one waiting to hear what was going to happen next. It was laughter and tears. It was the way my teacher lifted her glasses with the tip of her index finger and smiled at us before flipping to the next page.<br />It is the way my mom used to read to me. Every night she would tuck me in and lay down next to me. She'd open a book and we'd go on an adventure <em>together</em>. <br />More often than not, I fell asleep after half a hour. I fell asleep dreaming of other worlds; of a world where a courageous intelligent young girl such as Matilda outwitted tyrannical oppressive figures such as Trunchbull.<br /><br />So when I was looking for a book to read and my gaze landed on this one book, I <em>knew</em>.<br /><br />I knew I had to read it again. So I did.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="96448085524101926">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_774394463">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774394463" itemprop="url" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/774394463?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep" class="user" title="Casey ~Kaleidoscopic Killer of the Deep~ ">Casey ~Kaleidoscopic Killer of the Deep~ </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/109059.Matilda" title="Paperback 9780142410370" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep?shelf=tbr-with-the-boys" class="actionLinkLite">tbr-with-the-boys</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep?shelf=saw-the-movie" class="actionLinkLite">saw-the-movie</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep?shelf=with-the-wee-ones" class="actionLinkLite">with-the-wee-ones</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep?shelf=read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep?shelf=fantasy-is-fun" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-is-fun</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/12741656-casey-kaleidoscopic-killer-of-the-deep?shelf=leave-a-legacy" class="actionLinkLite">leave-a-legacy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer774394463">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7290884848081235429">This was the perfect reading experience for an out loud reread with my six year old. He absolutely adored the story and I had hoped he would because this is one of my absolute childhood favorites.<br /><br />We took our time and read this over two weeks with just small chunks each night. My little was cracking me up with his running commentary on the story and I realized very quickly that he is growing up so much faster than I realized.<br /><br />He was very focused on Matilda's family dynamic even after we meet the T</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7290884848081235429">This was the perfect reading experience for an out loud reread with my six year old. He absolutely adored the story and I had hoped he would because this is one of my absolute childhood favorites.<br /><br />We took our time and read this over two weeks with just small chunks each night. My little was cracking me up with his running commentary on the story and I realized very quickly that he is growing up so much faster than I realized.<br /><br />He was very focused on Matilda's family dynamic even after we meet the Trunchbull. He was surprised to learn that Matilda was left alone so frequently and it led to some very interesting breakfast conversations about some kids not having the same kind of family that we have. I am delighted that he is now at the age that he is making the connections between what we read in our books and our real life even when it is a book about a little girl that develops special kinetic powers.<br /><br />After we finished the book we watched the movie together and I made sure to tell him that frequently movies are not exactly the same as books so he shouldn't get upset if things don't happen the same. And I told him that the characters might not look the same as he had pictured them in his mind and that it was okay if that happened too. The only thing that really upset him in terms of differences between the book and the movie was that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[in the book, Matilda doesn't have her powers anymore because she is being challenged in other ways but in the movie she still has them at the end <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />My favorite comments from him as we read were:<br /><br /><em>"That's child endangerment"</em> &lt;- Said more than once and at one point wanted to know why no one had called the police.<br />*gasp* <em>"Mom... Matilda's daddy is sooo mean! MY daddy would NEVER rip up my book."</em><br /><br /><em>"What?! No mom, Miss Honey's aunt <strong>can't</strong> be the Trunchbull. She's horrible!!!"</em><br /><br />Now I get to look forward to reading this with my younger son in a few years!<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7290884848081235429">...more</a>

          </span>
