<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1310182772">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1310182772" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9329370-sidharth-vardhan" class="left imgcol" title="Sidharth Vardhan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451326831p2/9329370.jpg" alt="Sidharth Vardhan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1310182772?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9329370-sidharth-vardhan" class="user" title="Sidharth Vardhan">Sidharth Vardhan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9329370-sidharth-vardhan?shelf=best" class="actionLinkLite">best</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9329370-sidharth-vardhan?shelf=children-books" class="actionLinkLite">children-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9329370-sidharth-vardhan?shelf=7-uk-and-dependences" class="actionLinkLite">7-uk-and-dependences</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9329370-sidharth-vardhan?shelf=questioning-norms" class="actionLinkLite">questioning-norms</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1310182772">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer458498717643583457">It was a toss between this and 'Ulysses'. And 'The Sound and the Fury'* - Which, by the way, Matilda had read by age of five! and she liked it! Feeling embarrassed already? No? she could also tell you within seconds and without calculator; what is seventeen times nineteen. Can you? Can you?<br /><br />Not only is she a child prodigy; she also showed ability of telekinesis for sometime. Roald Dahl seems to have a message for both children and grown-ups. And it is quite clear; grown-ups need not always be rig</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText458498717643583457">It was a toss between this and 'Ulysses'. And 'The Sound and the Fury'* - Which, by the way, Matilda had read by age of five! and she liked it! Feeling embarrassed already? No? she could also tell you within seconds and without calculator; what is seventeen times nineteen. Can you? Can you?<br /><br />Not only is she a child prodigy; she also showed ability of telekinesis for sometime. Roald Dahl seems to have a message for both children and grown-ups. And it is quite clear; grown-ups need not always be right. We tend to assume that parents or teachers know what is the best for the children - because it is a very romantic thing to assume but often we see how wrong this assumption is:<br /><blockquote>
  <br /><em>“I'm right and you're wrong, I'm big and you're small, and there's nothing you can do about it.”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />Children are thus often forced to pay for their parent/guardians/ teachers' faults.<br /><br />And I have known parents who wish to avoid spending on their children's education, specially if they are girls. There are, you will agree, many teachers who detest their jobs and many often bully children.<br /><br />And, here a kid's genius need not necessarily be about books;it can art or sports or anything. <br /><br />And there is no lack of cases where children find themselves alone; fearing that they might not be understood: <br /><blockquote>
  <br /><em> "“What she needed was just one person, one wise and sympathetic grown-up who could help her.” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />And often children do revolt when they felt injustice is being done to them - they have a very strong sense of injustice, not yet used to it like grown-ups. They tend to do so by turning mischievous.<br /><br />Another good reason to read Dahl is that he teaches how to insult in civilized language:<br /><blockquote>
  <em><br />“You ignorant little slug!" the Trunchbull bellowed. "You witless weed! You empty-headed hamster! You stupid glob of glue!” </em>
</blockquote><br /><br />*Okay now, I know you are wondering how I tossed between three books. This is how it was - Heads it was Matilda, Tails I would toss again. If the coin had stayed up on its tip, it would have been 'The Sound and the Fury'. If it had stayed up in the air, it would have been 'Ulysses'. In the end it turned out to be Matilda. I mean what are the chances? It was as if something was pulling coin towards ground! Personally I was inclined towards reading Ulysses, but I had to do what coin told me to do. <br /><br />Looking back, it only seemed fair after my last read 'Lord of the Flies' failed the Bechdel test a big time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="458498717643583457">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1083811467">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17969764226328980149">So much fun to read, mainly because of the nostalgia, silly humour and mad-over-the-top characters - I especially loved evil Mrs Trunchbull and her Chokey and Matilda's awful parents. The only thing I wasn't crazy about was Matilda coming into her random powers too late in the story, also some of the kids sounded a little old for their age. Still it was an entertaining little read.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yKnXIILgOM6qNQnwok6Fb3Lm2mhHUe4Zqe0S5vI2PYBXXj3q1EYmowMaSEKq9UKpRcSTZgz1I8SJow5h5/uJyg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

Ze trekt er liever op uit met haar zelfgemaakte pijl en boog om langs de IJssel te z&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText4686476850321329962\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;In de tijd van de Hoekse en Kabeljauwse twisten is Kampen een belangrijke handelsstad, maar Hasse, dochter van een mandenvlechter, vindt het er maar druk en benauwd. Ze trekt er liever op uit met haar zelfgemaakte pijl en boog om langs de IJssel te zwerven. Haar ouders willen heel graag dat ze gaat trouwen, maar Hasse neemt haar eigen beslissingen. \nZe \'verbidt\' Jan van Schaffelaar, dat wil zeggen, ze redt hem van het schavot door met hem te trouwen. Samen trekken ze naar de Veluwe, waar hij als aanvoerder van een troep huurlingen de belangen van de hertog van Gelre behartigt. \n\nHasse geniet van het vrije ongebonden leven. Als jongen verkleed doet ze mee met de overvallen en als boogschutter weet ze het respect van de mannen af te dwingen.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">About Roald Dahl</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl"><img alt="4273" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1311554908p2/4273.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer11467823115229309426">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was Shot Down Over Libya. Today the story is published as "A Piece of Cake". The story, about his wartime a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11467823115229309426">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was Shot Down Over Libya. Today the story is published as "A Piece of Cake". The story, about his wartime adventures, was bought by the Saturday Evening Post for $900, and propelled him into a career as a writer. Its title was inspired by a highly inaccurate and sensationalized article about the crash that blinded him, which claimed he had been shot down instead of simply having to land because of low fuel.<br /><br />His first children's book was The Gremlins, about mischievous little creatures that were part of RAF folklore. The book was commissioned by Walt Disney for a film that was never made, and published in 1943. Dahl went on to create some of the best-loved children's stories of the 20th century, such as Charlie and the Chocolate Factory, Matilda and James and the Giant Peach.<br /><br />He also had a successful parallel career as the writer of macabre adult short stories, usually with a dark sense of humour and a surprise ending. Many were originally written for American magazines such as Ladies Home Journal, Harper's, Playboy and The New Yorker, then subsequently collected by Dahl into anthologies, gaining world-wide acclaim. Dahl wrote more than 60 short stories and they have appeared in numerous collections, some only being published in book form after his death. His stories also brought him three Edgar Awards: in 1954, for the collection Someone Like You; in 1959, for the story The Landlady; and in 1980, for the episode of Tales of the Unexpected based on "Skin".</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11467823115229309426">...more</a>

    </div>
